    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16457632927828596631">It's the week leading up to the Bicentennial celebration in Washington, D.C., and King Suckerman is the hot new blaxploitation film that's got everyone talking. Small-time dealer Dimitri Karras and his friend, record-store owner Marcus Clay, are out looking to score some weed when they stumble in on a big deal gone bad -- and pick up some cash that isn't theirs. Pursued by</span>
  <span id="freeText16457632927828596631" style="display:none">It's the week leading up to the Bicentennial celebration in Washington, D.C., and King Suckerman is the hot new blaxploitation film that's got everyone talking. Small-time dealer Dimitri Karras and his friend, record-store owner Marcus Clay, are out looking to score some weed when they stumble in on a big deal gone bad -- and pick up some cash that isn't theirs. Pursued by a trigger-happy gangster looking to settle the score, Dimitri and Marcus suddenly find that they're players in a savage game of cross and double-cross....<p>Brilliantly evoking the retrocool of seventies music, clothes, and movies, King Suckerman is bold, real, and violent -- a supercharged thriller in the hardboiled tradition of Jim Thompson, David Goodis, and Pulp Fiction. Here is George Pelecanos's strongest work to date -- a book that is certain to win him a whole new audience of admirers.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="16457632927828596631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_255832000" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/255832000" />
    <a title="Ted" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7213075-ted"><img alt="Ted" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101210p2/7213075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/255832000?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ted" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ted" href="/user/show/7213075-ted">Ted</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7213075-ted?shelf=reviews-liked">reviews-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7213075-ted?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7213075-ted?shelf=lit-american">lit-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7213075-ted?shelf=beach-fun-fiction">beach-fun-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7213075-ted?shelf=americana">americana</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255832000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4227703065927638177"><b>Revised playlists</b><br/>The playlists, as named below, <b>are available on Spotify.<br/>To listen on Spotify, see bottom of review</b>.<br/><br/><br/><br/><i>I've read about ten of George Pelecanos's novels. I've never picked up another book once I've started one of his, till I'm finished.</i><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442771122i/16276816.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>George Pelecanos, 2013</b><br/><br/>One of the best Pelecanos stories. This is the second of the D.C. Quartet series, published between 1996 and 2000. Takes place mostly over the July 4 weekend of 1976, that of the American Bicentennial. (I remember it well, we were</span>
  <span id="freeText4227703065927638177" style="display:none"><b>Revised playlists</b><br>The playlists, as named below, <b>are available on Spotify.<br>To listen on Spotify, see bottom of review</b>.<br><br><br><br><i>I've read about ten of George Pelecanos's novels. I've never picked up another book once I've started one of his, till I'm finished.</i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442771122i/16276816.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>George Pelecanos, 2013</b><br><br>One of the best Pelecanos stories. This is the second of the D.C. Quartet series, published between 1996 and 2000. Takes place mostly over the July 4 weekend of 1976, that of the American Bicentennial. (I remember it well, we were on the Mall for the fireworks with friends. Six months later I was a first-time father.)<br><br>His novels explore the Wash. D.C. crime scene; where he grew up, when he grew up. Very gritty. Sex, bad language, violence. But Pelecanos writes stories with real characters that you want to root for (if they're the good guys, of course). Also features some real mean dudes.<br><br>He always features both black and white characters, good, bad, and in between in both groups. <b>Oh, and ethnic characters too - Greek, of course - play a major role in almost all of his novels! As always, writing about what he knows.</b><br><br>One of the unique features of Pelecanos' novels is the way that popular music of the stories' eras is routinely featured in the narrative. This is not because the music plays a part in the plot, but rather because it helps set the story in its historical context. It can also get it playing in your head.<br><br>Having said that, I need to admit that I am typically only marginally familiar with much of the music that is mentioned in his stories. He obviously was not himself a big fan of top-40 music (nor was I) - his protagonists, if they are black, will be into R&amp;B/Soul music (or some brand of D.C. hip-hop in the more contemporary novels), while the white dudes will groove on album-oriented, progressive, or acid rock music.<br><br>When I read this book I decided to take notes on all the music that was mentioned. Frankly there is so much mentioned that I know I missed many songs and artists, but when I was done I had about 30-35 examples for both the white dudes and the soul brothers of the novel that I wanted to sample, or remember in some cases. I bought all this music from iTunes, and made four CDs out of it. The whole exercise was a great way to build up a little library, and become familiar with music from the mid-70's. Thanks George!<br><br><br><b>The original four playlists have been combined into two.</b> The order of songs has been changed. And several tracks have been added to both - these are shown in <b>bold</b>.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443074779i/16315333.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Jimi Hendrix flashing the peace sign prior to his performance of "The Star-Spangled Banner" at Woodstock, August 18, 1969.</b><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sjzZh6-h9fM">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sjzZh...</a><br><br>Seven of the new tracks are by Jimi Hendrix. Hendrix's music has its own sub-plot in the story, in which one of the main characters, who owns a record store, argues vehemently with a young employee over whether Hendrix's LPs should be filed with rock or soul music - this although they're both black. Older fellow says ROCK, younger man says SOUL. Fact is, older fellow is <i>probably</i> right for most of Hendrix's music, but not of course for all of it.<br><br>I've split six Hendrix tracks evenly between the two lists, with the Rock list getting songs from Hendrix's first album, <i>Are You Experienced</i>, and the Soul list picking up songs from that album and his last one, <i>Band of Gypsies</i>. I've put one of the new Hendrix tracks in the lead position on <i>both</i> playlists. I think this track, <i>Red House</i> (from <i>Experienced</i>), is a good example of one of his songs that really could be argued about back and forth. .<br><br><i>Are You Experienced</i> ... recorded in London in late 1966 &amp; early 1967, released in the U.K. in May '67, and in the U.S. in August (where it spent over two years on the Billboard 200) ... in 2005 ranked by Rolling Stone fifteenth on its list of the 500 Greatest Albums of All Time ... also that year, the record was one of 50 recordings chosen by the Library of Congress in recognition of its cultural significance to be added to the National Recording Registry. Writer and archivist Rueben Jackson of the Smithsonian Institution wrote: "it's still a landmark recording because it is of the rock, R&amp;B, blues ... musical tradition. It altered the syntax of the music ... in a way I compare to James Joyce's Ulysses." (Wiki) Probably the greatest debut album in pop music history.<br><br><i>Band of Gypsies</i> ... recorded live on January 1, 1970, at the Fillmore East in New York City ... Billy Cox on bass and Buddy Miles on drums ... "The album mixes funk and rhythm and blues elements with hard rock and jamming, an approach which later became the basis of funk rock ... the last full-length Hendrix album released before his death" less than nine months later (Wiki) A tragic end to one of the most creative musicians of the twentieth century.<br><br><br><br><b>King Suckerman - Rockers</b><br><br>1 <b>Red House, Jimi Hendrix</b><br>2 Midnight Rider, The Allman Brothers<br>3 <b>Foxey Lady, Jimi Hendrix</b><br>4 Tangerine, Led Zeppelin<br>5 <b>Highway Chile, Jimi Hendrix</b><br>6 Hey Lawdy Mama, Steppenwolf<br>7 Rock and Roll, Led Zeppelin<br>8 <b>Purple Haze, Jimi Hendrix</b><br>9 Mean Town Blues, Johnny Winter<br>10 Viva Tirado, El Chicano<br>11 Brown Eyed Girl, Van Morrison<br>12 Free Bird, Lynyrd Skynyrd<br>13 Dixie Chicken, Little Feat<br>14 Slide On Over Slinky, Rick Derringer<br>15 Reelin' In the Years, Steely Dan<br>16 Back to Get Ya, The J. Geils Band<br>17 Takin' Care of Business, Bachman-Turner Overdrive<br>18 It Wouldn't Have Made Any Difference, Todd Rundgren<br>19 <b>Too Much Time, Captain Beefheart</b><br>20 Madness, Mahogony Rush<br>21 We're an American Band, Grand Funk<br>22 Money, Pink Floyd<br>23 Karn Evil 9: 1st Impression, Pt. 2, Emerson, Lake &amp; Palmer<br>24 The Wizard, Uriah Heep<br>25 Two Trains, Little Feat<br>26 Thirteen, Big Star<br>27 <b>All the Young Dudes, Mott the Hoople</b><br>28 Sally Can't Dance, Lou Reed<br>29 The Fool and Me, Robin Trower<br>30 You Ain't Seen Nothing Yet, Bachman-Turner Overdrive<br>31 The Lamb Lies Down on Broadway, Genesis<br>32 <b>Kill Your Sons, Lou Reed</b><br>33 Any Major Dude Will Tell You, Steely Dan<br>34 Travelin' Shoes, Elvin Bishop<br>35 (Then Came the) Last of May, Blue Oyster Cult<br>36 Pretzel Logic, Steely Dan<br>37 <b>Man on the Silver Mountain, Rainbow</b><br>38 Master Builder, Gong<br>39 Bridge of Sighs, Robin Trower<br>40 Coney Island Baby, Lou Reed<br>41 Born to Run, Springsteen<br><br><br><b>King Suckerman - Soul Brothers</b><br><br>1 <b>Red House, Jimi Hendrix</b><br>2 War, Edwin Starr<br>3 <b>Power of Soul (Live), Jimi Hendrix</b><br>4 What's Going On, Marvin Gaye<br>5 (Don't Worry) If There's a Hell Below ... , Curtis Mayfeild<br>6 <b>Who Knows (Live), Jimi Hendrix</b><br>7 Maggot Brain, Funkadelic<br>8 <b>Them Changes, Buddy Miles</b><br>9 Give More Power to the People (For God's Sake), The Chi-Lites<br>10 The Bottle, Gil Scott-Heron<br>11 <b>The Wind Cries Mary, Jimi Hendrix</b><br>12 Never Never Gonna Give You Up, Barry White<br>13 Back to the World, Curtis Mayfield<br>14 For the Love of Money, The O'Jays<br>15 The Boss, James Brown<br>16 <b>Papa Was a Rolling Stone, The Temptations</b><br>17 Are You Man Enough, Four Tops<br>18 Down and Out in New York City, James Brown<br>19 A Joyful Process, Funkadelic<br>20 The Payback, James Brown<br>21 Hollywood Swinging, Kool &amp; The Gang<br>22 Little Child Runnin' Wild, Curtis Mayfield<br>23 Standing on the Verge of Getting It On, Funkadelic<br>24 Who Is He (And What Is He To You)?, Creative Source<br>25 You Sexy Thing, Hot Chocolate<br>26 Be Thankful For What You Got, William DeVaughn<br>27 It Only Takes a Minute Girl, Tavares<br>28 Theme From S.W.A.T., <b>Rhythm Heritage</b><br>29 I Can't Stand the Rain, Graham Central Station<br>30 Give Up the Funk, Parliament<br>31 Brown Eyed Girl, The Isley Brothers<br>32 Call Me (Come Back Home), Al Green<br>33 Gimme My Mule, The Commodores<br>34 Betcha By Golly Wow, The Stylistics<br>35 Bad Luck, Harold Melvin &amp; The Blue Notes<br>36 <b>Rock the Boat, The Hues Corporation</b><br><br><br><br>If I had to pick (luckily I don't) I'd take the soul music.<br><br><b>By the way, Pelecanos has a web site</b> -&gt; <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.george-pelecanos.com/">http://www.george-pelecanos.com/</a><br><br>There's a section on music (perhaps not updated very recently, but still good), a section on the work he did on The Wire, and other topics.<br><br><b>Spotify</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I know that most of the eastern hemisphere (except for Europe and Australia) does not yet have Spotify available. <div id="review_560263851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/560263851" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/560263851?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=pelecanos">pelecanos</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=crime-and-mystery">crime-and-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer560263851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4812915436679624749">It's 1976 and everyone's talking about King Suckerman, the new blaxploitation flick that's in the theaters. When Marcus Clay and Dimitri Karras wind up with a pile of cash after a drug deal gone wrong, everyone's after their hides, including a thug named Wilton Cooper and his gang, and an Italian named Tony Spags, who wants his money and his girl, who's shacking up with Karras. Can Clay and Karras give the money back without getting killed?<br/><br/>Here we are, the second book in George Pelecanos' DC Qua</span>
  <span id="freeText4812915436679624749" style="display:none">It's 1976 and everyone's talking about King Suckerman, the new blaxploitation flick that's in the theaters. When Marcus Clay and Dimitri Karras wind up with a pile of cash after a drug deal gone wrong, everyone's after their hides, including a thug named Wilton Cooper and his gang, and an Italian named Tony Spags, who wants his money and his girl, who's shacking up with Karras. Can Clay and Karras give the money back without getting killed?<br /><br />Here we are, the second book in George Pelecanos' DC Quartet. Pelecanos weaves a tale worthy of Elmore Leonard, set around our nations capital around the time a film called King Suckerman has everyone's attention. Pelecanos continues to develop the Washington DC of the Pelecanosverse, as Kemper calls it.<br /><br />It's a pretty straightforward crime tale about ill-gotten gains and murder. What makes it so good is Pelecanos' writing, specifically how well he develops his characters. You've got Cooper, Claggett, and the Thomas brothers, the killers of the piece, Spags and Tate, the lowlifes in over their heads, and Clay and Karras, the regular guys caught up in things. With the exception of the Thomas brothers, the characters are all well drawn and fairly realistic. Cooper was so slick I almost wanted him to live through everything. The action is pretty intense when it happens and the dialogue is almost as smooth as Elmore Leonard's in his prime.<br /><br />Interesting side note, I bought Eldorado Red by Donald Goines at the same time I bought this. Imagine my surprise when Goines makes a cameo appearance in the tale. <br /><br />Much like The Cut, I can't really find anything to complain about with King Suckerman. Pelecanos is quickly climbing the ranks of my favorite crime writers.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Also posted at Shelf Inflicted</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4812915436679624749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27544466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27544466" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27544466?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=signed-by-author">signed-by-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2019-reread">2019-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=dc-quartet">dc-quartet</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27544466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15799129051527998199">In the summer of ‘76 best buddies Marcus Clay and Demetri Karras are spending their free time playing pick-up basketball games while everyone in Washington DC is buzzing about the upcoming bicentennial celebration and a new blaxplotation flick called <i>King Suckerman</i>. As a Vietnam veteran and owner of a record shop Marcus is the more grown-up of the two while Demetri has no ambition beyond being a small time pot dealer. When Marcus accompanies Demetri to buy some weed the two end up in confrontati</span>
  <span id="freeText15799129051527998199" style="display:none">In the summer of ‘76 best buddies Marcus Clay and Demetri Karras are spending their free time playing pick-up basketball games while everyone in Washington DC is buzzing about the upcoming bicentennial celebration and a new blaxplotation flick called <i>King Suckerman</i>. As a Vietnam veteran and owner of a record shop Marcus is the more grown-up of the two while Demetri has no ambition beyond being a small time pot dealer. When Marcus accompanies Demetri to buy some weed the two end up in confrontation that makes them instant enemies of the dangerous Wilton Cooper and his gang of killers. <br /><br />The two main characters are the strongest part with Marcus being the hard worker who has a sense of responsibility that doesn’t allow him to let things slide. Demetri is the flip side of this as the slacker who despite being a decent guy deep down can always find an excuse to take the easy way out. Despite their differences Pelecanos creates a believable bond between the two, and he often uses similar types of people in his other novels. He also builds up a great cast of supporting players around them including the murderous Wilton Cooper.<br /><br />The other great aspect is Pelecanos’ ability to evoke the setting of Washington DC of a certain time. By using a mix of local history and geography combined with vivid descriptions of cars, clothes, food, and especially music, Pelecanos makes you feel like you’re driving in an Dodge Charger with the 8-track cranked up on your way to catch a late showing of <i>King Suckerman</i>.<br /> <br />It’s also incredibly patient novel that isn’t filled with action. It’s very easy to get caught up with Marcus and Demetri as well as the other characters as they just go about their lives with nothing huge happening. You can even forget that this is a crime novel at heart which makes the violence that much more shocking and awful when it does come.<br /><br />This is the first novel by George Pelecanos I ever bought, and I got my old 1998 paperback copy of it signed a few months back when I got to meet him at a book singing. That prompted this long overdue reread, and it gave me a new appreciation for what he does in these books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15799129051527998199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_751874539" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/751874539" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7668412-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329563818p2/7668412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/751874539?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/7668412-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781852427344" href="/book/show/926913.King_Suckerman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668412-andrea?shelf=crime-noir-pulp">crime-noir-pulp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668412-andrea?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668412-andrea?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer751874539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4369378028518146914">Look ma, no cops!<br/> <br/>As good as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/314022.Soul_Circus' title='Soul Circus by George Pelecanos' rel='nofollow noopener'>Soul Circus</a>, although I can't decide if the avalanche of 70's references in this one was distracting or not - they kept triggering either old memories (ah, how I pined for an orange Karmann Ghia but settled for a red Fastback; how I swooned over Harold Melvin and the Blue Notes <i>If You Don't Know Me By Now</i> and on and on...) or frustrated scramblings to link names with sounds (uh, Robin Trower, let's see, some sort of virtuoso guitarist, right? Damn, that's about all t</span>
  <span id="freeText4369378028518146914" style="display:none">Look ma, no cops!<br /> <br />As good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/314022.Soul_Circus" title="Soul Circus by George Pelecanos" rel="nofollow noopener">Soul Circus</a>, although I can't decide if the avalanche of 70's references in this one was distracting or not - they kept triggering either old memories (ah, how I pined for an orange Karmann Ghia but settled for a red Fastback; how I swooned over Harold Melvin and the Blue Notes <i>If You Don't Know Me By Now</i> and on and on...) or frustrated scramblings to link names with sounds (uh, Robin Trower, let's see, some sort of virtuoso guitarist, right? Damn, that's about all that trickles back.) Would be cool as an e-book with links to an integrated soundtrack for foggy brains, like mine, or just any reader who doesn't happen to have Pelecano's encyclopedic command of musical references, like me.<br /><br />Still, being able to pick up on all the notes is secondary; this is a juicy, pulsating crime novel that manages to get somewhere beyond the limits of pulp. No smart-ass detective to the rescue here; just a cast of players - the not-so-good, the bad, the stupid and the-just-happened to be there - all hanging, riding and writhing around the streets of DC. Pelecanos puts them all in the pot and lets them get on with it; what he doesn't do is waste his time and ours by judging them. And I do appreciate that!<br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4369378028518146914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2619670023?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Weston" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Weston" href="/user/show/313206-andy-weston">Andy Weston</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2619670023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1964726251693013139">It’s not difficult to see why Pelecanos spends more of his time screenwriting these days. His stories really need a soundtrack. He tells you what’s playing during this novel, so perhaps the way around it is to take time out and find and play the track. As with <i> The Deuce </i> it’s set in the seventies; the likes of the O-Jays, the Chi-Lites and Stylistics providing that soundtrack. Plus, it’s in dialogue that Pelecanos excels; such an easy transition to the screen. <br/>As opposed to New York though, thi</span>
  <span id="freeText1964726251693013139" style="display:none">It’s not difficult to see why Pelecanos spends more of his time screenwriting these days. His stories really need a soundtrack. He tells you what’s playing during this novel, so perhaps the way around it is to take time out and find and play the track. As with <i> The Deuce </i> it’s set in the seventies; the likes of the O-Jays, the Chi-Lites and Stylistics providing that soundtrack. Plus, it’s in dialogue that Pelecanos excels; such an easy transition to the screen. <br />As opposed to New York though, this is set in Washington D.C. and concerned with drug crime and racial tension, and has another great set of characters, most of them on the wrong side of the law. King Suckerman in a much hyped new movie, in the blaxploitation style of Shaft and Black Caesar. It’s showing at a drive-in the powerful opening scene. <br />Stand-out for me though, are the pair of villains he creates in the ex-con Wilton Cooper and natural born killer, Bobby Roy Clagget. <br />Tremendously entertaining. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3850124586844317918">It is the summer of 1976 and 'King Suckerman' is the title of a new film ("the one about the pimp?") that virtually every character in the novel is dying to watch. Taking place throughout Independence Day weekend of the Bicentennial Year, the novel portrays a melting pot of Washington D.C. denizens; a tapestry of races and a cauldron of ethnic criminality. Pelecanos' novel pulsates with the jive and vibe of the blaxploitation films it manifestly emulates and reveres. The facile and underwhelming</span>
  <span id="freeText3850124586844317918" style="display:none">It is the summer of 1976 and 'King Suckerman' is the title of a new film ("the one about the pimp?") that virtually every character in the novel is dying to watch. Taking place throughout Independence Day weekend of the Bicentennial Year, the novel portrays a melting pot of Washington D.C. denizens; a tapestry of races and a cauldron of ethnic criminality. Pelecanos' novel pulsates with the jive and vibe of the blaxploitation films it manifestly emulates and reveres. The facile and underwhelming plotting though is disappointing, as is the forced redemptive ending. Still, many electrifying moments and plenty of combustible badinage. </span>

<div id="review_160537411" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160537411" />
    <a title="Larry Bassett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3816725-larry-bassett"><img alt="Larry Bassett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390874855p2/3816725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160537411?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry Bassett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry Bassett" href="/user/show/3816725-larry-bassett">Larry Bassett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316695909" href="/book/show/2174695.King_Suckerman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3816725-larry-bassett?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3816725-larry-bassett?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160537411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7611105677928455568">Although I am a fan of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47387.George_P__Pelecanos' title='George P. Pelecanos' rel='nofollow noopener'>George Pelecanos</a>, I barely made it through the first third of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/307443.King_Suckerman' title='King Suckerman by George P. Pelecanos' rel='nofollow noopener'>King Suckerman</a> so I was amazed to read among the Wikipedia paragraphs:<br/> <br/><blockquote><i>King Suckerman</i>, set in the 1970s and generally regarded as the fans' favorite, introduced the recurring theme of basketball in Pelecanos' fiction. Typically, he employs the sport as a symbol of cooperation amongst the races, suggesting the dynamism of D.C. as reflective of the good will generated by multi-ethnic pick up games. <br/>From <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Pelecanos'>http://en.</a></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText7611105677928455568" style="display:none">Although I am a fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47387.George_P__Pelecanos" title="George P. Pelecanos" rel="nofollow noopener">George Pelecanos</a>, I barely made it through the first third of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/307443.King_Suckerman" title="King Suckerman by George P. Pelecanos" rel="nofollow noopener">King Suckerman</a> so I was amazed to read among the Wikipedia paragraphs:<br /> <br /><blockquote><i>King Suckerman</i>, set in the 1970s and generally regarded as the fans' favorite, introduced the recurring theme of basketball in Pelecanos' fiction. Typically, he employs the sport as a symbol of cooperation amongst the races, suggesting the dynamism of D.C. as reflective of the good will generated by multi-ethnic pick up games. <br />From <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Pelecanos">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_P...</a> </blockquote><br /><br />The “fans’ favorite”? I can’t imagine. But, I still end up giving it three stars, only two for the first half but four for the last.<br /> <br />I have read quite a bit of early and recent Pelecanos but the first half of <i>King Suckerman</i> has to be the least satisfying segment of his storytelling that I have read so far. Mostly missing the usual Pelecanos character development, the early part of the book focuses on clothes, cars, time period, music and language. These are all standard and normally enjoyable Pelecanos but in this case they seemed to replace the storyline. Maybe I just have a bad attitude about this book; when I was haunting the library stacks looking for Pelecanos books I had not yet read, I passed by this book repeatedly, and left it on the shelf. I am glad to have finally read it and look forward to seeing its role as the second book in the D.C. Quartet series.<br /> <br />Oh, yea. In spite of the fact that Pelecanos’ references are often based on real songs and cars and places I don’t think <i>King Suckerman</i> was an actual movie. At least I couldn’t track it down with Google.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7611105677928455568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_29940468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29940468" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/945136-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599667575p2/945136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29940468?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/945136-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29940468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9192782874618257862">This is Pelecanos tribute to 1970's blaxploitation flicks. And what better way to do that than to write a book in the very style of the waaay over the top movies it skewers? Almost all of the characters seem to have walked directly from the screenings of Shaft, Superfly and the Mack onto the pages of this book. Pelcanos even keeps the soundtrack tight by constantly referencing 70's music staples and some one hit wonders that only someone who lived it could remember. He skillfully recreates the e</span>
  <span id="freeText9192782874618257862" style="display:none">This is Pelecanos tribute to 1970's blaxploitation flicks. And what better way to do that than to write a book in the very style of the waaay over the top movies it skewers? Almost all of the characters seem to have walked directly from the screenings of Shaft, Superfly and the Mack onto the pages of this book. Pelcanos even keeps the soundtrack tight by constantly referencing 70's music staples and some one hit wonders that only someone who lived it could remember. He skillfully recreates the excesses of the Wash. D.C. club scene as a counter-point to the protest and militancy of the street and public protests. The patriotic Bicentenial celebrations versus the still burnt out and desolate inner cities versus the comfortable suburbs in Maryland and Virginia. Saturday Night Fever meets the Black Panthers meets Superfly. Nobody wins and nobody is without sin. Its a time and place; 1970's pre-gentrification D.C., that I lived through and Pelecanos does it both over the top and exactly right. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9192782874618257862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2102493358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2102493358" />
    <a title="Aditya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15583553-aditya"><img alt="Aditya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600956683p2/15583553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2102493358?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aditya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aditya" href="/user/show/15583553-aditya">Aditya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316204460" href="/book/show/11968876-king-suckerman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2102493358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18033251762985403207"><b>Mini Review</b><br/><br/>King Suckerman is the quintessential Pelecanos novel. The painstakingly detailed world Pelecanos creates has a remarkable vibrancy placing the reader in seventies Washington; however the protagonists that inhabit it are unfortunately one dimensional and are left to wallow in a derivative plot. He really nails down the setting; the street lingo, the culture, the atmosphere is a tantalizing recreation of a different time and a tangible presence throughout the book. But the plotting has </span>
  <span id="freeText18033251762985403207" style="display:none"><b>Mini Review</b><br /><br />King Suckerman is the quintessential Pelecanos novel. The painstakingly detailed world Pelecanos creates has a remarkable vibrancy placing the reader in seventies Washington; however the protagonists that inhabit it are unfortunately one dimensional and are left to wallow in a derivative plot. He really nails down the setting; the street lingo, the culture, the atmosphere is a tantalizing recreation of a different time and a tangible presence throughout the book. But the plotting has always been bare bones in most of Pelecanos novels and this one is no different, so in spite of all his brilliant world building his novels seldom are as gripping as they could be.<br /><br />Wilton Cooper as the unpredictable, depraved, sociopathic villain is easily the best character and brings an unhinged energy and a desperate urgency with him every time he appears on the pages. If the protagonists were half as interesting I would have thought about pushing my rating higher. All this ends up being is a middle of the road crime novel for the genre faithful with too much indulgent stuffing and senseless violence to ever truly appeal to the wider mainstream audience. Rating - 3/5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18033251762985403207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16874055692486542179" style="display:none">So, I finally finished Pelecanos' D<br />C. Quartet, and I completely read it out of order, starting with The Sweet Forever, then into Shame the Devil, followed by the first book, The Big Blowdown, and finally this one. So of course I wish I read them in order. But there is something to bouncing around in time through D.C., and I think something is powerful and interesting to conclude with this funky book in the series. The major characters are all really just being introduced in this one, and the hope that exists here is a better note to go off on then the rather dismal turn of events found in the other books. As a whole, this and The Sweet Forever-my first Pelecanos book-are my favorite. He is just so damn good.</span>

    <a title="Thomas Loudermilk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70396296-thomas-loudermilk"><img alt="Thomas Loudermilk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503412557p2/70396296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2145254304?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Loudermilk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Loudermilk" href="/user/show/70396296-thomas-loudermilk">Thomas Loudermilk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70396296-thomas-loudermilk?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2145254304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14520917388949587544">"King Suckerman" is the second installment of Pelecanos's 'DC Quartet' series. It finds close friends Dimitri Karras and Marcus Clay just before the bicentennial, Clay just getting started with his chain of record stores and Karras living the bachelor high-life, seeling marijuana to make ends meet. Just when Clay thinks that his hell-raising years are behind him, he finds himself at Karras's side during a drug deal gone wrong. When they remember the bag of cash that Clay snagged during their hur</span>
  <span id="freeText14520917388949587544" style="display:none">"King Suckerman" is the second installment of Pelecanos's 'DC Quartet' series. It finds close friends Dimitri Karras and Marcus Clay just before the bicentennial, Clay just getting started with his chain of record stores and Karras living the bachelor high-life, seeling marijuana to make ends meet. Just when Clay thinks that his hell-raising years are behind him, he finds himself at Karras's side during a drug deal gone wrong. When they remember the bag of cash that Clay snagged during their hurried escape, Clay and Karras realize that coming after them is Wilton Cooper and his crew who are out for blood as much as they are out for money.<br /><br />On the surface, "King Suckerman" is a fast-paced and effective crime thriller. But deeper down its an intensely detailed study of Washington D.C. in the circa-1976. The intersectionality of culture, the explosion of African-American culture in film and music, and the visceral reality of life on the streets. It's at once a fully-realized cultural study and a can't-put-it-down thriller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14520917388949587544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1894659885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894659885" />
    <a title="Nigel Bird" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4939292-nigel-bird"><img alt="Nigel Bird" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442532979p2/4939292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894659885?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nigel Bird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nigel Bird" href="/user/show/4939292-nigel-bird">Nigel Bird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894659885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6629448798447383442">‘Don’t be wishin’ me no good luck. It’s all luck man. If there’s one thing I learned overseas, that’s it.’<br/><br/>I’m usually a sucker for a Pelecanos. He ranks right up there as one of my favourites. Suckerman, however, took a good while to win me over.<br/><br/>It’s a novel that harks back to the nineteen seventies and deals with some cracking modern American themes. There’s a blistering soundtrack, the shadows of Vietnam, guns, drugs, basketball, race, gangsters, movies and loyalty.<br/><br/>The opening is a cold-bloode</span>
  <span id="freeText6629448798447383442" style="display:none">‘Don’t be wishin’ me no good luck. It’s all luck man. If there’s one thing I learned overseas, that’s it.’<br /><br />I’m usually a sucker for a Pelecanos. He ranks right up there as one of my favourites. Suckerman, however, took a good while to win me over.<br /><br />It’s a novel that harks back to the nineteen seventies and deals with some cracking modern American themes. There’s a blistering soundtrack, the shadows of Vietnam, guns, drugs, basketball, race, gangsters, movies and loyalty.<br /><br />The opening is a cold-blooded killing at a drive-in movie. It’s ruthless and exciting and almost too brutal to allow for an early connection with the characters.<br /><br />From there we meet our protagonists, Greek waster Dimitri Karras and Marcus Clay, who enter into a drugs deal and cross swords with the murderers from the drive in. Things go wrong at the connect and Karras and Clay walk away with a large amount of cash and a gangster’s girlfriend who’s looking for an easier life of getting high and watching TV.<br /><br />What follows are the inevitable consequences of stealing from a bunch of thugs and an inevitable showdown that is as tense and exciting as they come.<br /><br />It took me a good while to find my bearings. There are a lot of people to get to know. There’s a lot of information about TV, films, sport and music to digest and I didn’t immediately connect to anyone other than Clay.<br /><br />At around the mid-point the author began to wind me in. The diverse threads began to tighten into one thick strand. Insights into the lives of Karras and Clay won me over. The consequences of the early crime spill over to hurt the innocent and this allows windows into souls. There are subtle hits like the categorisation of a Hendrix album, the responsibilities of parenthood and the connections and mindsets forged in war. There are even appearances from Nick Stefanos and his grandfather to ice the cake.<br /><br />By the finale, I was emotionally hooked.<br /><br /><br />This may not be my favourite book by the author, but I’d recommend it nonetheless. It’s a cut above a hell of a lot of fiction even if it is a little below par.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6629448798447383442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_131124374" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131124374" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3779897-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294937750p2/3779897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131124374?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/3779897-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781852427344" href="/book/show/926913.King_Suckerman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131124374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5978238097957793865">George Pelecanos was about to give up on writing when he decided start a book in his spare time, almost as a lark. These beginnings show, for good and for ill, in <i>King Suckerman</i>, the novel he ended up completing. Whereas in many of Pelecanos's books, he takes a single act of violence and carefully examines its meanings and repercussions, here there's a senseless, gruesome murder in the first few pages, and the book continues apace, with many stomach-turning bits of violence following. Perhaps it</span>
  <span id="freeText5978238097957793865" style="display:none">George Pelecanos was about to give up on writing when he decided start a book in his spare time, almost as a lark. These beginnings show, for good and for ill, in <i>King Suckerman</i>, the novel he ended up completing. Whereas in many of Pelecanos's books, he takes a single act of violence and carefully examines its meanings and repercussions, here there's a senseless, gruesome murder in the first few pages, and the book continues apace, with many stomach-turning bits of violence following. Perhaps it's simply the setting--<i>Suckerman</i> takes place in the '70s, when Washington, DC, was quickly becoming a much scarier place. Or perhaps it's Pelecanos paying homage to the Blaxploitation genre that infuses both the plot and the milieu of the narrative.<br /><br />In keeping with its casual composition, some of the characters seem more sketched out than in his previous book <i>The Big Blowdown</i>. Here Pelecanos has found the crime writer's tool of extremely eccentric antagonists, with one character bordering on grotesque. When old characters from <i>The Big Blowdown</i> start to pop up, it's jarring, as if a character from an old black-and-white wartime drama strolled onto the screen during <i>Shaft</i>.<br /><br />All that said, the rock solid prose almost never falters, and the buildup to the climax is miss-your-subway-stop good. There's still a sentimental streak to his writing, but it, like so much about Pelecanos's novels, is growing on me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5978238097957793865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15794897404776005007">Fun, crammed with music and smoke and basketball, reeking of the 70's, you'd expect this crime story to be a thoughtless joyride. Likewise, the decision to frame the thing as <i>King Suckerman</i> (in the book, <i>King Suckerman</i> is a too-real movie about a pimp) will stump and fascinate me for a while. This story was not too-real, and yet at moments it was totally alive. Great, quick </span>
  <span id="freeText15794897404776005007" style="display:none">Fun, crammed with music and smoke and basketball, reeking of the 70's, you'd expect this crime story to be a thoughtless joyride. Likewise, the decision to frame the thing as <i>King Suckerman</i> (in the book, <i>King Suckerman</i> is a too-real movie about a pimp) will stump and fascinate me for a while. This story was not too-real, and yet at moments it was totally alive. Great, quick read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17973630609792707167">Holy shit. After Shoedog I couldn’t hold off staying on the Pelicanos train. And after a second dose of his tight prose, well illustrated tragic characters, I am super hooked on this...sensitive pulp? Is that a genre? <br/><br/>King Suckerman has everything I loved about shoedog but with a Hitchcockian Everyman in a bad position kind of twist. Throw some record store geeks and their music into the mix and an overarching blaxploitation film as a sort of thematic chorus for the whole piece. I loved this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText17973630609792707167" style="display:none">Holy shit. After Shoedog I couldn’t hold off staying on the Pelicanos train. And after a second dose of his tight prose, well illustrated tragic characters, I am super hooked on this...sensitive pulp? Is that a genre? <br /><br />King Suckerman has everything I loved about shoedog but with a Hitchcockian Everyman in a bad position kind of twist. Throw some record store geeks and their music into the mix and an overarching blaxploitation film as a sort of thematic chorus for the whole piece. I loved this book. <br /><br />Starting to see more and more nods to character beats/relationships that would later shoe low up in The Wire, but having a main “hero” like Clay who is a small business owner in a bad spot humanizes the work immediately as opposed to the usual spread of underworld characters who reveal their humanity in spite of their dark deeds(though Suckerman has some of that as well...) <br /><br />I’m not getting off this train anytime soon. The Sweet Forever is next and I can’t wait. A prime example of the genre that hits all the notes you could want. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17973630609792707167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Josh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/852867-josh"><img alt="Josh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201672729p2/852867.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2292548818?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh" href="/user/show/852867-josh">Josh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440225959" href="/book/show/797258.King_Suckerman">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2292548818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11720075014043551271">This book has plenty of what I like best and least about Pelecanos. In the minus column, he writes terrible women characters (women can only be supportive nurturers, sex bombs, or sex bomb/nurturers), nearly every single person in his books has an implausibly encyclopedic knowledge of music and film (I don't think a room full of drug dealers in '70s D.C. would be Big Star fans, for example), and his geographic descriptions are too hilariously detailed (I know he grew up in D.C., but do we really</span>
  <span id="freeText11720075014043551271" style="display:none">This book has plenty of what I like best and least about Pelecanos. In the minus column, he writes terrible women characters (women can only be supportive nurturers, sex bombs, or sex bomb/nurturers), nearly every single person in his books has an implausibly encyclopedic knowledge of music and film (I don't think a room full of drug dealers in '70s D.C. would be Big Star fans, for example), and his geographic descriptions are too hilariously detailed (I know he grew up in D.C., but do we really need exact street addresses, cross-streets, descriptions of nearby businesses, etc., like we're asking for directions or searching Mapquest or something?). Fortunately, we also get one of his strangest and most exciting plots, some truly frightening villains, a skillful slow build of tension and dread, and an empathetic lament for the wildly different ways violence, drugs, and apathy can damage good people and make bad people worse. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11720075014043551271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2323032476893318905">This is book #2 of the D.C. Quartet by George Pelecanos. I had previously read book #1, "The Big Blowdown," and was 1/3 of the way through books #4, "Shame the Devil," when this book came in as a library transfer. I was somewhat confused at first because one of the main characters, Dimitri Karras, is carefree and single here but is a married parent with a child in book #4. The book is an homage to black exploitation movies, and is chock full of characters who are good guys with flaws and bad guy</span>
  <span id="freeText2323032476893318905" style="display:none">This is book #2 of the D.C. Quartet by George Pelecanos. I had previously read book #1, "The Big Blowdown," and was 1/3 of the way through books #4, "Shame the Devil," when this book came in as a library transfer. I was somewhat confused at first because one of the main characters, Dimitri Karras, is carefree and single here but is a married parent with a child in book #4. The book is an homage to black exploitation movies, and is chock full of characters who are good guys with flaws and bad guys, some of whom aren't too bad and many of whom are thoroughly evil. The characters are interesting, the plot keeps you on the edge of your seat, and the dialog is crisp. Like many of his novels he weaves in music, fast cars and culture of the day (the novel takes place during the Bicentennial Celebration in D.C.).</span>

After a while, you question whether you really need to know what's on the radio every time someone gets in a car. <div id="review_3353823223" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3353823223" />
    <a title="Stew Hamblin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112800262-stew-hamblin"><img alt="Stew Hamblin" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3353823223?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stew Hamblin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stew Hamblin" href="/user/show/112800262-stew-hamblin">Stew Hamblin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3353823223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11659023069965436625">Pelecanos is a sober writer who never wastes a word. He does months of research before sitting down to write. King Suckerman stands out in his oeuvre because of its looseness-but this only enhances the book. The plot and characters move lightly, even when packing heat. You could tell he was having fun with writing this book. He spent his first couple of books mastering his craft, and he's now confident enough to experiment without losing his budding style. He's like a guitarist who's moved past </span>
  <span id="freeText11659023069965436625" style="display:none">Pelecanos is a sober writer who never wastes a word. He does months of research before sitting down to write. King Suckerman stands out in his oeuvre because of its looseness-but this only enhances the book. The plot and characters move lightly, even when packing heat. You could tell he was having fun with writing this book. He spent his first couple of books mastering his craft, and he's now confident enough to experiment without losing his budding style. He's like a guitarist who's moved past memorizing scales and licks and can now make up his own. King Suckerman is not a good overall representative of his work, but it's a great gateway into the best crime writer of the last 30 years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11659023069965436625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3116448725" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3116448725" />
    <a title="Colleen Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39102040-colleen-kennedy"><img alt="Colleen Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514917647p2/39102040.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colleen Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colleen Kennedy" href="/user/show/39102040-colleen-kennedy">Colleen Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3116448725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9937773469280926917">A Tarantino-esque narrative with nasty criminals, a sociopathic killer, drug deals gone really wrong, some cool cats, and a killer soundtrack. Like Tarantino, too, it is a white man fetishizing the coolness of 1970’s Black culture, and especially in this case, Blaxploitation films. It’s violent, mindless, and, despite its flaws, it’s also incredibly fun to watch the average guys try to get away with the spoils of a shootout, and Pelecanos creates some memorable characters. (I started the year wa</span>
  <span id="freeText9937773469280926917" style="display:none">A Tarantino-esque narrative with nasty criminals, a sociopathic killer, drug deals gone really wrong, some cool cats, and a killer soundtrack. Like Tarantino, too, it is a white man fetishizing the coolness of 1970’s Black culture, and especially in this case, Blaxploitation films. It’s violent, mindless, and, despite its flaws, it’s also incredibly fun to watch the average guys try to get away with the spoils of a shootout, and Pelecanos creates some memorable characters. (I started the year wanting to read more books set in Washington, DC and his collection of neo noir set in different DC decades appealed to me for this reading project.) </span>
  <a data-text-id="9937773469280926917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uRm2KM/kqLuL4yoEY09XlLTgrgtH/BDMvbVeB8EhZuFz4ZgGbGed6zFTKFxESgbILrFn6cz5g94kIHegCK74xQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4GMdculOYmDiekfA+hgjEgs8jdtvAdBlYU1TrWgZjukqmzNcSs1XMFjKRZjdHXJOkW1EOeQEQ3f42HoKoZYQzQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/17549479.George_Pelecanos">About George Pelecanos</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/17549479.George_Pelecanos"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1522121097p3/17549479.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/17549479.George_Pelecanos">George Pelecanos
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,275
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9137802296711221655">George Pelecanos was born in Washington, D.C., in 1957. He worked as a line cook, dishwasher, bartender, and woman's shoe salesman before publishing his first novel in 1992.<br/><br/>Pelecanos is the author of eighteen novels set in and around Washington, D.C.: <i>A Firing Offense</i>, <i>Nick's Trip</i>, <i>Shoedog</i>, <i>Down by the River Where the Dead Men Go</i>, <i>The Big Blowdown</i>, <i>King Suckerman</i>, <i>The Sweet Forever</i>, <i>Shame the Devi</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9137802296711221655" style="display:none">George Pelecanos was born in Washington, D.C., in 1957. He worked as a line cook, dishwasher, bartender, and woman's shoe salesman before publishing his first novel in 1992.<br /><br />Pelecanos is the author of eighteen novels set in and around Washington, D.C.: <i>A Firing Offense</i>, <i>Nick's Trip</i>, <i>Shoedog</i>, <i>Down by the River Where the Dead Men Go</i>, <i>The Big Blowdown</i>, <i>King Suckerman</i>, <i>The Sweet Forever</i>, <i>Shame the Devil</i>, <i>Right as Rain</i>, <i>Hell to Pay</i>, <i>Soul Circus</i>, <i>Hard Revolution</i>, <i>Drama City</i>, <i>The Night Gardener</i>, <i>The Turnaround</i>, <i>The Way Home</i>, <i>The Cut</i>, and <i>What It Was</i>. He has been the recipient of the Raymond Chandler award in Italy, the Falcon award in Japan, and the Grand Prix du Roman Noir in France. <i>Hell to Pay</i> and <i>Soul Circus</i> were awarded the 2003 and 2004 <i>Los Angeles Times</i> Book Prizes. His short fiction has appeared in <i>Esquire</i>, <i>Playboy</i>, and the collections <i>Unusual Suspects</i>, <i>Best American Mystery Stories of 1997</i>, <i>Measures of Poison</i>, <i>Best American Mystery Stories of 2002</i>, <i>Men from Boys</i>, and <i>Murder at the Foul Line</i>. He served as editor on the collections <i>D.C. Noir</i> and <i>D.C. Noir 2: The Classics</i>, as well as <i>The Best Mystery Stories of 2008</i>. He is an award-winning essayist who has written for <i>The New York Times</i>, <i>The Washington Post</i>, <i>GQ</i>, <i>Sight and Sound</i>, <i>Uncut</i>, <i>Mojo</i>, and numerous other publications. <i>Esquire</i> called him "the poet laureate of the D.C. crime world." In <i>Entertainment Weekly</i>, Stephen King wrote that Pelecanos is "perhaps the greatest living American crime writer." Pelecanos would like to note that Mr. King used the qualifier "perhaps."<br /><br />Pelecanos served as producer on the feature films <i>Caught</i> (Robert M. Young, 1996), <i>Whatever</i>, (Susan Skoog, 1998) and <i>BlackMale</i> (George and Mike Baluzy, 1999), and was the U.S. distributor of John Woo's cult classic, <i>The Killer</i> and Richard Bugajski's <i>Interrogation</i>. Most recently, he was a producer, writer, and story editor for the acclaimed HBO dramatic series, <i>The Wire</i>, winner of the Peabody Award and the AFI Award. He was nominated for an Emmy for his writing on that show. He was a writer and co-producer on the World War II miniseries <i>The Pacific</i>, and is currently at work as an executive producer and writer on David Simon's HBO dramatic series <i>Treme</i>, shot in New Orleans.<br /><br />Pelecanos lives with his family in Silver Spring, Maryland.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9137802296711221655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_307439'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/307439.The_Big_Blowdown?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Big Blowdown (D.C. Quartet #1)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/17549479.George_Pelecanos?origin=series_works\">George Pelecanos<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.03 avg rating &mdash; 2,572 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1996\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer18029869023355847559\">Washington DC, 1946. For two local young men, Pete Karras and Joey Recevo, the easiest way to find work after the war is by providing a little muscle for a local boss who runs a protection racket with the Mafia. The trouble with Pete Karras is that h<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText18029869023355847559\" style=\"display:none\">Washington DC, 1946. For two local young men, Pete Karras and Joey Recevo, the easiest way to find work after the war is by providing a little muscle for a local boss who runs a protection racket with the Mafia. The trouble with Pete Karras is that he is just too soft on his fellow immigrants, and the last thing the boss wants is for his mob to get soft.
